For years, Konami's Metal Gear franchise


has stood in a league of their own when


it comes to narrative ambition in video


games. With each new installment, Hideok


Khjima has consistently pushed the


boundaries of interactive storytelling,


strengthening the argument that video


games are a legitimate and powerful


storytelling medium. His latest works,


Death Stranding, and its sequel, Death


Stranding: 2 on the Beach, only


reinforce that legacy, with upcoming


titles like OD and Fizzant, poised to


carry it even further. But the origin of


this groundbreaking vision wasn't born


out of creative freedom. It came from


chaos. In a 1999 interview with Nice


Games via Schmuplations, Kojima


reflected on how the very first Metal


Gear game came to him under turbulent


circumstances.


Quote, "Konami said that they wanted a


game made around the theme of war, but


the development had a troubled history.


Several of Konami's veteran developers,


who had released many hit games before I


joined the company, had been working on


this war game for 2 years now, but it


wasn't going anywhere. They'd create


something, then scrap it, create


something, and scrap it again. There was


a sort of legend at Konami that if you


got involved in this project, you'd up


demoted or transferred." I have no idea


why they kept continuing it, but I think


as a company, Konami just really wanted


to have a war game. So, that was how the


project came to me. That was where it


started from. What I was fixated on


making in the scope of a war game was an


escape game. You know that old movie,


The Great Escape. I thought it would be


awesome to make a game built around a


concept like that of trying to escape


from somewhere. But when I told the


senior devs on the team about my idea,


they were very dismissive. Quote,


"There's no games like that." I was


still a new planner at Konami, so I


guess no one was inclined to listen to


what I had to say. There was just zero


motivation from the start. It was like,


"What do I have to do here? Do I have to


start beating people up?" By and by, the


situation only degraded further into


passive aggressive resistance. I got to


the point where I was so fed up with


working at a corporation like this that


I was ready to quit Konami altogether.


Eventually, with the help of a


sympathetic colleague and a single


moment of innovation, the now iconic


exclamation mark that appears when an


enemy spots the player, everything


changed.


That one mechanic convinced the team


that Kojima's vision had merit. And with


that spark, Metal Gear was born.


You can agree or disagree with Kojima on


a number of things, but what is


undeniable is that Metal Gear has long


been a trailblazer in elevating


cinematic storytelling in video games.


That said, there's one common critique


that persists even among admirers of the


series. The story can be incredibly hard


to follow. Kojima is known for throwing


unexpected narrative complexities, so


it's no surprise that keeping up with


the full arc of the saga can be a


challenge for many. To that effect,


we're revisiting our full story series


of the Metal Gear games we covered 8


years ago. But this time, we have


significantly expanded it and that too


in glorious 4K and 60 frames per second.


This is not a mere compilation as we've


gone back and patched in several


enhancements and updates and even


corrected several mistakes in our


original series. So before the launch of


Metal Gear Delta Snake Eater and the


10th anniversary of Metal Gear Solid 5:


The Phantom Pain's release, we will take


a look at the complete series from start


to finish in chronological order in


order to make it easier hopefully for


those who are not entirely familiar with


the franchise's lore and narrative, as


well as for those whose memories just


need to be refreshed. We will tackle the


series in the following order. Metal


Gear Solid 3: Snake Eater, Metal Gear


Solid Portable Ops, Metal Gear Solid


Peace Walker, Metal Gear Solid 5 Ground


Zeros, Metal Gear Solid 5: The Phantom


Pain, Metal Gear, Metal Gear 2 Solid


Snake, Metal Gear Solid: The Twin


Snakes, Metal Gear Solid 2: Sons of


Liberty, Metal Gear Solid 4: Guns of the


Patriots, and finally, Metal Gear


Rising: Revengeance.


And obviously there will be spoilers


ahead, but you already knew that. In


chapter 1 of our recap of the Metal Gear


franchise, we will look at the events


surrounding Virtuous Mission and


Operation Snake Eater in Metal Gear


Solid 3, which is the very first game in


the Metal Gear chronology. quote, "If I


had wanted to release MGS3 within a year


of releasing MGS2, the easiest way of


doing that would be to pick up where


MGS2 ended using the same engine, the


same game system, even the same


characters." Hideokima stated in an


interview with Gamespy in 2004, quote,


"I guess Electronic Arts and many other


companies do this, but if I did that, it


would be no fun at all. quote, "I


decided that MGS3 would be about


survival, and I started to think about


how survival would work in the game. The


game takes place in the 60s, and if the


game was going to be about survival, I


decided it had better take place in the


jungle." Kojima further added, "That


decision to ground the game in a jungle


survival setting would go on to define


not only the gameplay mechanics, but


also Metal Gear Solid 3's backdrop.


Snake Eater takes place in 1964 when the


United States of America and the USSR


are right in the middle of the Cold War.


In 1962, a scientist named Soolov, who


is the Soviet Union's foremost weapons


developer appears on the scene. So, who


is Salof? Solof is a rocket scientist


who played a key role in the Soviet


Union's Vastto program where he was


responsible for designing the


multi-engine cluster that powered the


Vastto A1. Despite wanting to stay in


aerospace, Soolov was reassigned to


weapons development, sparking a


one-sided rivalry with fellow scientist


Alexander Leonovich Gran, whom we will


talk about later. Sov was working on a


quote unique weapon when he got so


scared of its abilities. He defects to


the US, requesting that his family also


be allowed to defect with him. And this


is where Major Zero comes in. Zero,


whose real name is David O along with


the CIA, helps Soolov to defect to the


USA. But due to the long travel


distance, Solov gets burned out and he


has to be admitted to a hospital.


However, things change considerably


after the fateful events of the Cuban


missile crisis, and the US agrees to


return Solov back to the USSR in secret


as part of the negotiations between the


two nations. In return, the Soviets will


remove their missiles from Cuba. He's


taken back to a facility called the


OKB754


Soalov Design Bureau, where he is tasked


with finishing work on the weapon that


he had previously been working on.


However, the Soviets Nikita Kruev's grip


on power weakened. Tensions rose between


him and other factions within the Soviet


military. A specific faction plotted to


dispose of him and replace him with


Alexe Kosigan and Leoned Brev. To


prevent Sokov's weapon from falling into


their hands, the KGB relocated him to a


factory in Rasvet and made it clear


they'd kill him if needed. Now, let's


take a moment to focus on Major Zero and


the rest of his support team. Zero is


arguably one of the most pivotal figures


in the entire Metal Gear universe,


though his true motivations, and the


far-reaching consequences of his actions


will unfold gradually throughout this


story series. In his early years, Zero


forged a close bond with the boss, who


we'll explore in greater detail soon,


and the two served together in the


British Special Air Service. He later


joined MI6 where he was cenamed simply O


before transitioning to the CIA where he


became known as Zero, a name that would


come to symbolize both order and control


in the shadows of global politics. The


boss, also known as Joy, founded the


legendary Cobra unit in 1942 during


World War II. Comprised of elite


soldiers known as the fear, the end, the


pain, the fury, and the sorrow. Each


member embodied a specific human


emotion, giving the unit a mythic,


almost symbolic presence on the


battlefield. Under her leadership, the


Cobras played a crucial role in securing


victory for the Allied forces, earning


the boss the revered title of mother of


special forces. Another key detail in


her story is that during the invasion of


Normandy, the boss gave birth to the


Sorrow's child. After being critically


wounded by gunfire, she was forced to


undergo an emergency cesarian section. A


procedure that left her with a distinct


snake-like scar across her abdomen.


Trust Hideokima to blend history,


emotion, and mystery well so seamlessly.


Defying the wishes of the director of


central intelligence, Major Zero went on


to form the elite Fox unit alongside the


boss. Together, they assembled a small


but highly specialized team. paramedic,


a brilliant medical adviser with an


encyclopedic knowledge of cinema, and


Sigant, a cuttingedge expert in weapons


and military technology. And that just


about covers the Fox units. Well,


almost. There's one more name you need


to know. John, also known as Jack and


cenamed Naked Snake. He's the central


figure of Metal Gear Solid 3 and the


character players step into throughout


the mission. A highly skilled operative,


Jack became the boss's disciple in the


1950s, training under her in close


combat, espionage, and eventually


co-developing the iconic CQC system. He


also witnessed the 1954 Bikini ATL


hydrogen bomb test, which well left him


sterile. Though they parted ways, the


boss left a deep and lasting imprint on


Jack, shaping him into the soldier and


man he would become. Both Zero and Snake


held the boss in the highest regard, not


just for her skills, but for her ideals.


Her dream of a unified world would


become the ideological foundation and


eventual point of divergence for both


men. There are also a couple of


intriguing details worth keeping in


mind. Paramedic had a deep interest in

considerable power and influence to

Metal Gear Solid 3 tells, the rise of


Snake and his transformation from a


soldier to worldrenowned legend. We now

Ops.


In chapter 1, we talk about the virtuous


mission and operation snake eater, the


sacrifice of the boss, and how the


operative known as naked snake was given


the title of big boss. In chapter 2, we


will talk about Snake's growth as a


legend and his next step towards


accepting the mantle of big boss through


portable ops.


Metal Gear Solid Portable Ops is a


strange game. strange because Hideo


Khojima has given rather mixed signals


about it being canonical. In some


interviews, he stated that while the


overall story is canon, certain parts of


it are not. Yet, the game's marketing


trailers during the game's release


boldly promoted it as the quote missing


link. And interviews around its launch


reinforced that narrative. However,


during the leadup to The Phantom Pain,


Cojima made no mention of Portable Ops


as part of the official Metal Gear saga,


and it was notably absent from the


series's official timeline as well.


Quote, "I always say this will be my


last Metal Gear. But the games in the


series that I've personally designed and


produced, Metal Gear on the MSX, Metal


Gear 2, Metal Gear Solid 1, 2, 3, 4, and


Peacewalker, and now Metal Gear Solid 5


are what constitute a single Metal Gear


saga. With Metal Gear Solid 5, I am


finally closing the loop on that saga.


In that sense, this will be the final


Metal Gear Solid. Even if the Metal Gear


franchise continues, to me, this is the


last Metal Gear, Cojima said in an


interview with IGN in 2015.


This is kind of shocking as many


gameplay elements from Portable Ops were


later refined and used in Peace Walker


and The Phantom Pain. Interestingly


though, Konami has since recognized the


events of Portable Ops as canon. In the


2023 Masterbook series provided with the


release of Metal Gear Solid Master


Collection Volume 1, the game was


officially included in the timeline of


Canonical Events. This shift is notable,


especially since, as you'll see in our


story breakdown, the events of Portable


Ops directly set the stage for Peace


Walker. Without the events of Portable


Ops, the story of Peace Walker would


feel incomplete.


With that out of the way, let's dive

In chapter 3, we'll talk about the

Quote, "Solid Snake's story line has

it was a time when these theories were


actually thought to be effective. And


now, we're paying the price. We've still


got tons of nuclear weapons scattered


all over the world. to fully grasp the

understand the chain of events that


brought us here. So, before we dive into

reverted to Hungarian control from


Romania during World War II. Hungary


initially allied with Nazi Germany as


part of the Axis powers, but was later

World War II, Allied bombers attacked

escape, he was knocked down in the

words he remembered in his native


language. Soon after, foreign troops

In chapter 4 of our recap series, we


covered the downfall of MSF, the


destruction of Mother Base, and how a


mysterious individual named Skullface


wre havoc on Big Boss and company. In


chapter 5, we will look at the events of


Metal Gear Solid 5: The Phantom Pain and


the rise of the legend of Big Boss in


the form of Venom Snake, also known as


Punished Snake. Metal Gear Solid 5: The


Phantom Pain is a very different entry


in the series compared to the previous


games. Beyond being an openw world Metal


Gear, Kojima's storytelling approach


also saw a significant shift. While the


core cutscenes were still present, much


of the narrative unfolded quote on the


ground. During missions to extract


targets or gather intel to fully grasp


the game's lore, players had to go


beyond the usual expectations of a


linear single player experience, piecing


the story together from the world


itself, cassette tapes, and key


cutscenes. In a 2014 interview with Game


Informer, Cojima explained how he


approached this in The Phantom Pain


while revealing his appreciation for


Grand Theft Auto 5. quote, "I haven't


been able to play that many games. I do


try to watch people playing them. I want


to play GTA badly, but I haven't found


the time to play Grand Theft Auto 5."


With that in mind, we're calling Metal


Gear Solid 5 an open world game. That's


the way we're bringing it out. But


ideally, I want to create a game that


even people like me that don't have too


much time to sit down and play the game


for a long time can play through it.


There will be long missions. There will


be rather short missions. There will be


kind of episodic chapters like a TV


series. And if you have time, you play


these chapters. When you have time, you


build up your mother base. Eventually,


your character starts developing. And


when you put it all together, it becomes


a huge story. That's the way I try to


develop it. Cojima said back then, this


approach laid the foundation for the


complex and layered narrative that would


define the Phantom Pain story. And what


a story it is. In many ways, The Phantom


Pain's lore feels refreshingly unique,


though much of it is tucked away in


cassette tapes, onfield conversations,


and moments open to interpretation. Once


you piece it all together, it becomes


clear that Cojima was at the height of


his creativity here. Metal Gear Solid 5:


Phantom Pain is a story told through a


flashback. Big Boss is shown standing in


a room in front of a mirror in a


location known as Outer Heaven with the


sounds of gunfire roaring in the


background. He picks up a cassette tape.


It begins to play and the screen fades


out. It's 1984. A plane dives sharply


and crashes with someone breathing


heavily in the background. Though the


event isn't shown on screen, it's a


detail worth keeping in mind.


Mayday, mayday. Controls unresponsive.


Tower, do you read

There are, however, still a lot of


important story threads that the Phantom


Pain resolves. When Paz was in


Skullface's captivity, she reveals that


Zero was hiding in a top floor,


windowless, unlisted room of a cipher


controlled apartment building in Hell's


Kitchen. 10th Avenue. The only way in


was through a secret staircase from room


702, one floor below. The entire


building was staffed by cipher


operatives disguised as ordinary tenants


with heavy surveillance, emergency

However, Skullface deceived her. He had

When Skullface finds out the location of


Zero through Paz, he sent him a certain

thus to Zero. The pin was infected with


a certain parasite strain. And when Zero


picked up the pin by mistake, he was


immediately infected with that virus.


Zero did not die, but his health


degenerated rapidly over the next few

conversation, Zero reveals the extent of


his failing health, admitting that no


treatment can save him. Surprisingly, he

for what he did to Big Boss during the

that he never intended for Snake to be


his enemy. In fact, he only wanted Big


Boss on his side as a friend, something


that Big Boss will never know. In order


to take revenge against Skullface and


save the real big boss, Zero hinged on


secrecy, misdirection, and the help of


two unlikely allies, Ocelot and Eva.


After the destruction of Mother Base,


Zero launched a disinformation campaign


to hide the fact that Big Boss had


survived, relocating him to a secure


military hospital in Dellia, Cyprus. Eva


oversaw the medical transfer, while


Ocelot was tasked with keeping Big Boss


hidden and safe for as long as


necessary. Zero also revealed a backup


plan. The Phantom of Big Boss, a mental


copy who could operate in his place,


giving the real Big Boss time to recover


without the world knowing he was


incapacitated. It was a rare moment of


cooperation between Zero and Ocelot.


Both setting aside their differences for


Big Boss's survival. With Miller,

game. Knowing Kazz's loyalty to Big


Boss, he kept his location secret.


Instead, offering a trusted


intermediary, who is Ocelot, to relay

"V has come too." Zero insisted the


worst actions had been carried out by


unsupervised elements of his own

the dark to maintain leverage and ensure

When the Phantom Big Boss was set to


awaken, Zero and Ocelot agreed on the


code phrase, "V has come too," as the


signal to mobilize everyone involved.


Both the real Big Boss and his Phantom


had been in comas for 9 years. But


judging from his conversation with

recovered first. From the start, Big


Boss knew Zero was aiding him in a way,

explaining the plan to create a perfect


double who would serve as Big Boss's


public face. Through induced hypnogogia,

This wasn't just to fool Cipher. It was

even he would undergo self-hypnosis,


erasing conscious knowledge of the

something he will never know throughout


his lifespan.

dismantling the system entirely. The

After accepting the title of Big Boss

The wreckage from Sahalanthropus, would

Venom's role as Big Boss has come to an

Diamond Dog's emblem morphs into an


Outer Heaven logo. This transition


suggests that several years have passed,


bringing the timeline forward to 1995,


the point where the events of the


original Metal Gear unfold. During the


pre-release period of The Phantom Pain,


Hideok Khjima was hyping the game as a


missing link between the original Metal


Gear and how it showcases men turning


into demons. The game does indeed show


the downfall of Big Boss. Not in the way


most Metal Gear fans expected, but it


shows the degeneration of Big Boss's


ideals in a rather indirect way. Just


like Big Boss felt he was betrayed by


his nation when he was manipulated into


eliminating the boss during MGS3, he too


took one of his best men and turned him


into a pawn for himself. The world would


never know the deeds and actions of the


boss. And that is exactly what will


happen with Venom Snake 2. Just like


Skullface, whom history has forgotten,


Venom 2 is a phantom. Everything he's


done exists in a strange limbo. Real in


action, but false in identity. His


entire legend, every accomplishment, now


belongs to the real big boss. In a way,


the real Big Boss betrayed not just his


best man, but us, the players. Because,


as Cojima intended, we the players are


Phantom Big Boss. Through this, the game


mirrors Big Boss's own fall from grace,


showing how he used his most trusted man


in the same way he himself felt used


during the events of Metal Gear Solid 3.


By the end, the real big boss had become


a demon, a man stripped of remorse,


willing to sacrifice his best ally to


serve his own vision.


Kojima's vision for the Phantom Pain


revolved around the theme of race, not


just in the biological sense, but as a


combination of factors that define and


drive humanity. One of those factors was


language, which became a major motif in


the game. It explored how the loss of


language could strip away one's


identity, driving a man like Skullface


into madness. The game was also a


meditation on loss. Kazahhiro Miller


would never be the same after losing his


limbs and later learning the truth about


Big Boss. A betrayal that was already


seated in Peacewalker when Cass acted


against him. Though he did genuinely


care for him in the years that followed.


Skullface, for his part, is a man erased


from history, destined never to be


mentioned again in the series. But the


greatest loss belongs to the medic. He


lost his very identity, sacrificing


himself to preserve the legend of Big


Boss, unknowingly setting himself up to


be used once more. Played like a fiddle


11 years later. And that about wraps up


the story of the Phantom Pain. While the


Phantom Big Boss spreads the legend far


and wide, and the real Big Boss is


building outer heaven, the Patriots AI


won't remain silent. All of this sets


the stage for the arrival of a legendary


hero, Solid Snake.


[Music]


In chapter 5 of our Metal Gear Saga


recap, we explored the momentous events


of The Phantom Pain and how they connect


to the series's future. Now, in chapter


6, we're jumping ahead 11 years to 1995


in time to meet the one and only legend


himself, Solid Snake. Before we dive


into the events of Metal Gear 1987, it


is worth noting that stealth as a genre


was virtually unheard of at the time,


and the industry had never seen anything


quite like Metal Gear before. As we


discussed in chapter 1, Cojima had to


work hard to convince his team that such


a game could succeed. However, the


development of Metal Gear was far from


straightforward. In an interview


published by MSX magazine on May 12th,


2005, later transcribed by Tumblr user


the Arkhound, Kojima revealed that he


actually disliked the MSX, the very


console the game was released on. Quote,


"There are many developers who came from


the MSX. Even in Konami, there are many


people who would tell me that they


joined the company because of Metal


Gear, but the truth is that I actually


hated the MSX when I joined Konami."


Kojima stated, quote, "Back in my


college days, I thought about joining


the games industry since I spent most of


my free time at the video arcades, but


the MSX hardly crossed my mind. When I


joined Konami, I was only thinking of


doing arcade and Famicom games, and I


had many ideas for those platforms. But


for some reason, I was assigned to do


MSX games instead. It was difficult


working on the original MSX since


sprites would disappear when you line


them up next to each other, and the


graphics weren't monochromatic. It was


pretty painful, he further added. He


also revealed the difficulties he faced


while developing for that console.


Quote, "Back then, I think you could


only move in six directions. Six


directions was going to be impossible,


but even reducing it to just four was


too restricting. We had no choice but to


make a game that could be done without


enemies. And that's what allowed me to


develop Metal Gear. In fact, he even


faced difficulties integrating bullets


into the game." Quote, "They wouldn't


come out horizontally either. There were


five function keys, so we thought about


using each of them. The F4 key, for


example, would bring up the transceiver.


Simultaneously, pressing one key and


another was unthinkable on a controller,


Cojima further added. Little did he


know, those early struggles were setting


the stage for a mission that would


change everything. Operation Intrude in


313, the beginning of Solid Snake's


journey in Metal Gear. The story of the


Phantom Pain ends in the year 1984 with


both Big Boss and his body double Venom


Snake working in different capacities to


make the dream of Outer Heaven a


reality. The events of the first Metal


Gear transpire in 1995, and a lot has


happened in that time. Unfortunately,


not much has been explained officially


about what happened during those 11


years, but we can make some educated


guesses based on hints from previous


chronological entries. After the events


of the Phantom Pain, Big Boss went into


hiding under a new identity, slowly but


surely building outer heaven. Venom,


meanwhile, now carrying the title of Big


Boss, focused on expanding Diamond Dogs


and spreading the legend of Big Boss


across the globe. At some point, Big


Boss almost completed his work on Outer


Heaven, and Venom's Diamond Dogs were


absorbed into it. To stay hidden from


Cipher, now known as the Patriots, fully


controlled by an AI network, and to


avoid arousing suspicion, Big Boss


tricked them and returned to the United


States. There, he somehow became a


commander of Foxhound, the special unit


he had originally formed after the


events of Portable Ops. Big Boss's dream


to turn Outer Heaven into a soldier's


refuge, has warped beyond recognition.


After no longer believing in the boss's


will, he is now a man transformed, a


monster to the point that he has now


become a wararmonger. By 1995, Outer


Heaven is now an established, heavily


fortified state. But no one in the world


really knows who their legendary


mercenary leader is. To the outside


world, Big Boss is the leader of the


reformed Foxhound unit. By this time,


Solid Snake, one of the genetic super


soldiers to come out of the La Aanton


project, has now become a member of the


Foxhound unit. Interestingly, Snake,


with an IQ of 180 and fluent in multiple


languages, doesn't have much of a


background story. As noted during the


events of the Phantom Pain, he never


actually left the United States when he


was a teenager. And when he would grow


up, he would be trained by two people.


big boss who would train him for CQC and


then under the toutelage of Kazahhira


Miller who Snake calls Master Miller.


Miller served as Snake's drill


instructor and has played the role of


mentor to him and the two share a close


bond. Interestingly, it's assumed that


Big Boss and Cass eventually made peace


as Cass went on to join the very unit


commanded by Big Boss. Little did Cass


know he was about to be played like a


damn fiddle all over again. And we


mustn't forget one very important


character. After the events of Portable


Ops, Frank Joerger was rescued once


again by Big Boss, who then took him and


his sister Naomi Hunter back to the


United States. Interestingly, it's


unclear whether this was the real Big


Boss or Venom. But given that the former


was in hiding at the time, it was most


likely Venom who saved them. Frank would


later join Foxhound and would be given


the highest commenation, Fox, resulting


in his code name, Grey Fox. Frank and


Solid Snake would go on to become close


allies, forging a strong friendship


through their shared battle and


experiences.


Well, with all the major pieces in


place, Big Boss sets his plan into


motion. Western states receive


intelligence that a weapon of mass


destruction is being constructed in


outer heaven, a nation in South Africa,


200 km north of Garsburg. As such, to


assess the situation and any potential


threat, Foxhound agent Gray Fox is sent


by Big Boss, commander of the Foxhound


unit, to outer heaven. The mission,


though, quickly goes off course. The US


government loses contact with Gray Fox,


who gets captured. And in his last


transmission, which serves as a warning,


he only communicates a message


consisting of just two words: Metal


Gear. It is at this point that rookie


Foxhound operative Solid Snake is tapped


for a follow-up mission by Big Boss,


Operation Intrude in 313. His objectives


to locate and rescue Grey Fox and to


assess the meaning behind the words


metal gear. His only backup is support


from Foxhound leader Big Boss, who


remains in constant contact with him


over the radio from his position in the


United States. Once Snake is inserted


into the site via underwater insertion,


he manages to use Supreme stealth skills


and his wits, all in an attempt to glean


as much information as he can about the


base and the facilities there and to


learn of the whereabouts of Gray Fox.


Snake at last manages to find the


location of Gray Fox thanks to the help


of local resistance leader Kyle


Schneider. Now, let's hold our horses


for just a moment. Who exactly is Kyle


Schneider? Schneider was once a member


of Outer Heaven, serving as an architect


and an engineer. However, as the


organization became increasingly


consumed by war and violence, he lost


his family. Disillusioned, he went


underground and eventually founded a


resistance movement opposing Outer


Heaven, rising to become its leader.


Given his knowledge of Outer Heaven's


layout, Schneider aided Snake by


revealing a complicated plan. Snake


would need to intentionally allow


himself to be captured. Once that


happened, Big Boss would contact him


with instructions to break through a


weakened wall, leading him to Gray Fox.


Of course, Big Boss already knew all


about Outer Heaven. Unsurprisingly so.


The Foxhound agent then reveals to him


the meaning of his last cryptic message.


Metal Gear, cenamed TX55, is actually a


bipeedal walking tank capable of


launching a nuclear strike from any


terrain and surface anywhere in the


world, making it a lethal weapon of mass


destruction and far beyond the nuclear


capabilities of most other international


actors. It's crewed by a single pilot


and armed with twin Vulcan guns, a laser


cannon, multiple missile launchers, and


a blast furnace cannon. Its armor is


reinforced with tungsten and a special


heatresistant ceramic for extra


durability. When preparing to fire a


missile, the TX55 deploys a stabilizing


leg at the rear to anchor itself,


ensuring steady and accurate nuclear


launches. Snake realizes the situation


is more dire than imagined and Gray Fox


tells him that it is imperative that


Metal Gear be destroyed before it's


activated. Snake's instructed with


tracking down Dr. Drago Petravich


Madnar, a Russian scientist and the


developer of Metal Gear. The doctor and


her daughter were abducted by Outer


Heaven personnel while the duo were in


the USA. He is the only person who would


know how to destroy it, who should also


be held prisoner somewhere in Outer


Heaven. However, the path to the doctor


won't be easy as Snake would need to


take down the Outer Heaven's Formidable


boss unit comprising of Shot Maker and


Machine Gun Kid, Firetrooper, Dirty


Duck, as well as fighting off some


seemingly invincible cyber known as


Bloody Brad, and several armored


vehicles such as Hind Bulldozer, and a


tank. Although this unit doesn't have a


lot of backstory, let's talk about what


we do know about them. Shotmaker was


once a Spetznaz operative during the


Soviet era before turning to mercenary


work. Machine Gun Kid, a former member


of the British Army's SAS special


forces, followed a similar path into


mercenary life. Firetrooper, originally


part of a German military unit,


specialized in flamethrower combat.


Dirty Duck was the leader of a group


called Eggplant, while Bloody Brad, also


known as Arnold, and designated TX11


were two cybernoid units developed by


Dr. Madnar. Snake defeats these foes at


different points in the mission, but


during the encounters, he notices


something suspicious. His stuff has been


planted with a transmitter, as if


someone wanted to track his every move.


Wasting no time, he disposes of it and


presses on with his mission. When Snake


finally reaches the location where Dr.


Madnar is supposed to be held, he


instead encounters a decoy posing as the


scientist. It's a setup meant to trap


him, but Snake sees through the ruse,


evades the danger, and makes his escape.


Later, Snake is contacted by Jennifer, a


member of the resistance and a former


medical staff member of Outer Heaven,


who reveals the location of the real Dr.


Madnar. In exchange, Snake agrees to


help her by rescuing her brother, who's


held hostage within Outer Heaven.


Snake finally meets the scientist, but


Madnar does not prove to be cooperative.


And he informs Snake that he will only


share the details about Metal Gear and


how the bipeedal tank can be destroyed


if Snake first rescues his daughter


Ellen, who is also being held captive in


Outer Heaven. With the help from Diane,


a resistance member and a skilled intel


gatherer, Snake is able to track down


and successfully rescue Ellen, who


informs him that her father was being


made to develop Metal Gear TX55 under


duress with her being used as a hostage.


With Ellen rescued, Dr. Madnar finally


informs Snake of Metal Gear's location


and the exact method of destroying it,


placing plastic explosives on its feet.


Snake begins to make his way to the


hanger where Metal Gear is being kept.


But he also starts to notice things are


starting to go wrong. The enemies seem


to be too informed of his movements, far


more than they should be, even when


taking all of the surveillance on the


facilities into account. Meanwhile, Big


Boss, who's been in constant contact


with him via radio, appears to be acting


erratic and strange, at one point even


asking Snake to abort the mission. Snake


is then contacted by Schneider, who's


about to reveal the true identity of the


man behind Outer Heaven. But his


connection drops. Outnumbered,


outsmarted, and with no resources on his


side, Snake nevertheless manages to make


his way to where Metal Gear TX55 is


being kept and manages to destroy the


bipeedal tank, neutralizing the threat.


This however initiates Outer Heaven's


self-destruct sequence, prompting Snake


to hasten his escape, in the course of


which he finds himself coming face to


face with the leader of Outer Heaven's


facility, who is finally revealed to be


Big Boss himself. Big Boss informs Snake


that the entire mission that he had been


sent on had been a decoy, with Snake


himself being sent to only create a


distraction. Big Boss, however,


seemingly underestimated Snake's


resourcefulness and never expected him


to have come as far as he had. Big Boss


declares his dream of a haven for


soldiers. A dream which had started with


MSF and grown with Diamond Dogs, acting


as one of the nuclear powers in the


world, outstripping even the West and


USSR so that it can continue remaining


defiant in the face of opposition. Faced


with betrayal and the threat of


geopolitical upheaval, Snake nonetheless


manages to defeat the legendary soldier


in a ruthless battle. It's also safe to


assume that before dying, Big Boss


handed the boss's bandana to Solid


Snake, something he had held on to ever


since recovering it during the events of


the Phantom Pain.


He escapes and calls Foxhound, informing


them that the threat is neutralized and


that the operation intrude in 313 had


been a success. It is unknown to him,


however, that the big boss he defeated


was not really Big Boss at all. The man


who Snake defeated was actually a body


double. Yes, it was none other than


Venom Snake, who had been acting on Big


Boss's commands as the leader of Outer


Heaven. He was a man who lived as a


phantom of the legendary Big Boss and


has now died as one, too. However, it's


worth noting that based on our


interpretation of the Phantom Pain's


ending, Venom was likely betrayed by Big


Boss when Operation Intrude in 313's


ending event was set into motion,


essentially sending him into a life or


death battle against Solid Snake. The


real big boss, it turns out, is still


alive, and he recognizes Snake as a


viable threat. He isn't done with Snake,


and his dream of creating the perfect


soldier's refuge isn't over either.


Outer Heaven was just one cog in his


machinery and served as a mere


distraction for the Patriots so that he


can buy time and complete work on his


own version of Outer Heaven. Big Boss


leaves the USA and Foxhound and goes


into hiding. Outer Heaven is ultimately


destroyed by NATO with the entire


fortress reduced to rubble. Tragically,


many innocent people lose their lives in


that attack. Among the survivors, such


as Gray Fox and Schneider, and others


are rescued by the real big boss,


setting the stage for the Zanzibar Land


incident. Since this was the first Metal


Gear game, Hideok Khjima didn't openly


discuss its themes like he would with


later major entries. However, based on


the story, one theme stands out above


all else. Betrayal. The real big boss


not only betrayed Solid Snake, but also


his phantom, Venom Snake, setting the


stage for his next major confrontation


against the Patriots. By this point, he


had become much like the very system


that once used the boss and discarded


her legend. In short, Big Boss has


transformed into a monster, willing to


do anything to achieve his vision of a


world where the fires of war will never


extinguish. At the same time, the


Patriots AI were quietly studying every


detail and patterns of the Outer Heaven


infiltration.


Well, and with that, we are done with


the story of Metal Gear. In chapter 7,


we will speak about how Solid Snake will


face an even bigger challenge against


the real big boss when we infiltrate


Zanzibar Land.


In chapter 6 of our Metal Gear Saga


recap, we examined how the real big boss


betrayed both Solid Snake and his


phantom, Venom Snake, only for his


insurrection to end in failure. Chapter


7 picks up with Solid Snake stepping


back into the fray, this time to


confront a new threat. It's fascinating


to look back at the origins of Metal


Gear 2: Solid Snake, and even more so


when we uncover rare historical


material, like an interview from 1990.


Transcribed by Tumblr user the Arkhound,


this piece from the August 1990 issue of


MSX magazine features an anonymous


Konami employee discussing how the


concept for Snake's second outing came


to life. While the magazine never names


the individual, the tone and depth of


the responses suggest that it was very


likely Hideokima himself. Quote, "The


reason why this game was made can be


attributed to a certain employee within


Konami around the time when SD Snatcher


was in the end of its development. While


I was taking the train ride home, he


made a rather passionate request." "Why


aren't you making a Metal Gear sequel?


If you made one, I would certainly buy


it." Up to that point, I had no


intention of developing a sequel to


Metal Gear. By the time I got home, I


already came up with the story and


synopsis in my head. The employee also


explained why cutscenes are important.


Quote, "While working on the original


Metal Gear, we had to delete all the


cutscenes we prepared for the game since


they went over the ROM capacity. It was


a pretty painful experience. This time,


we thought about the inclusion of


cutscenes from the very beginning and


managed to secure the required ROM size.


Cutcenes are important since they play a


key role as far as an experienced games


is concerned," the employee stated.


Again, judging from later interviews,


the responses line up almost exactly


with how Kojima would speak about his


work. Regardless of the mystery around


the interviewe's identity, it's a


fascinating glimpse into the game's


birth. This employee already had the


core story for Metal Gear 2: Solid


Snakes sketched out during a short train


ride home. It's 1999, and by the end of


the 20th century, the Cold War is


beginning to thaw out. It looks like


relations between the US and USSR are


beginning to stabilize a bit and that


the threat of imminent nuclear


proliferation may be a thing of the


past. On the surface of it, things look


to finally be taking a turn for the


better. However, this is more like the


calm before the storm. In this period,


the world has hit an oil crisis and


efforts to develop an alternative source


of energy are bearing no fruit. Amidst


all of this, Czech scientist Dr. Kio


Marv bio-engineers a new species of


algae known as oilix. That may be the


answer to these problems. On his way to


a demonstration of the newly engineered


strain algae in the United States,


however, he goes missing. Two years


prior, Zanzibar Land emerged in Central


Asia in 1997 as a powerful self-declared


democratic military regime. Its sudden


rise began with an armed uprising that


caught the attention of CIS whose forces


centered around Russia quickly mobilized


to suppress it. However, Zanzibar land


proved to be no ordinary adversary.


Recruiting elite mercenaries from across


the globe, the regime fortified its


territory into an impenetrable


stronghold. The CIS army suffered


repeated defeats and before long,


Zanzibar land had declared full


independence. This conflict, defined by


the dominance of hired soldiers, became


known as the mercenaries war, and the


nation itself gained a fearsome


reputation as an armed fortress state.


NATO realizes that there may be a


connection here. Zanzibar Land's leaders


may have nuclear capabilities.


Meanwhile, intelligence suggests that


its leaders plan to hold the world


hostage by controlling the supply of


oil. How do they plan to do this? Well,


it turns out that Dr. Marv was abducted


by none other than the masterminds of


Zanzibar Land by controlling the oilix


algae while simultaneously also holding


the spectre of looming nuclear war over


everyone's heads. Zanzibar Land plans on


truly becoming one of the greatest


powers on the global stage. to address


the situation. Colonel Roy Campbell,


yes, the same Campbell Big Boss


encountered during the events of


Portable Ops, who later served in Delta


Ops and now commands the Foxhound unit,


only calls Saul the Snake out of


retirement. Snake's mission this time is


to rescue Dr. Kio Marv. Snake will of

Master Miller, and yes, our very own


Cass, who has been brought on as a


consultant for Snake's mission. George


Casler also serves as an adviser,


providing Snake with intelligence


briefings on his enemies in Zanzibar.


With the mission codenamed Operation


Intrude F014,


the operation is set into motion. When


Snake is inserted into Zanzibar Land, he


comes into contact with Holly White, an


American freelance journalist who


developed a passion for literature early


in life. Beneath the surface, however,


Holly led a double life. She's an


undercover CIA operative posing as a


journalist who tells Snake she'll be


providing support for him during the


mission. As Snake makes his way towards


Dr. Marv's location, he's attacked by a


figure known only as Black Ninja. Black


Ninja was part of a special forces unit


consisting of technologically enhanced


ninja-like soldiers secretly formed by


NASA, who envisioned conflicts in outer


space in the future. Absurd, yes, and a


little over the top, but hey, that's a


Metal Gear for you. Anyways, Black Ninja


now functions as a mercenary whose


allegiances lie with Zanzibar Land. It


is then revealed that Black Ninja is


none other than Kyle Schneider, who is


the leader of the resistance against Big


Boss's regime in Outer Heaven. When his


true identity is revealed to Solid


Snake, the former resistance leader


reveals some startling facts.


Unbeknownst to Solid Snake, when he left


outer heaven after completing his


mission four years ago, NATO launched a


massive bombardment, including nuclear


strikes against the fortified state,


afraid of their potential for


troublemaking in the future. Outer


Heaven was completely wiped from the


face of the Earth, killing anyone that


was still in the area, regardless of


whether or not they had ties to Big


Boss's regime, including many war


orphans and resistance members. This


incident was largely covered up and


hidden from the media, and very few

reveals to Snake that the leader of


Zanzibar Land is actually none other


than Big Boss himself. Snake, who


doesn't know that the man he defeated 4

well, obviously shocked by this news.


Big Boss acrewed a huge number of allies


over the past four years, using NATO's


ruthless attacks against outer heaven as


motivation for many of them, including


Schneider, and established his foothold


in Zanzibar land to keep his dream of a


soldier's refuge alive. Snake defeats


Schneider in battle, but the encounter


proves fatal for the latter. With his

whereabouts.


With this crucial new piece of


information, he moves forward with his


mission. He infiltrates a facility in


Zanzibar land where he finds himself

past, Dr. Madnar, who's apparently been


kidnapped again to work on a new Metal


Gear. This time known as Metal Gear D.


Metal Gear D is an 8 1/2 m tall single


pilot nuclearcapable bipeedal weapon


protected by powerful plates and


heatresistant ceramic armor. It can


reach speeds of 45 km per hour with a


sensor range of 12,500 m and a 6,500 kW


power output. Its arsenal includes


conventional guns, missile pods, and up


to six short two mid-range nuclear


missiles. Madnar has also been


conscripted to work on smaller


non-nuclear Metal Gear units called


Metal Gear Gustaf or Metal Gear G,


similar to the Walker Gear units that


Skullface had worked on over a decade


ago. now. However, production isn't


completed yet. Matnar confirms to Snake


that Big Boss is indeed still alive and


well and now heads Zanzibar land. Matnar


reveals the location of where Dr. Marv


is being held and urges Snake to rescue


him, warning that Marv is suffering from


heart disease. Snake, faced with the


prospect of trudging across a desert to


save Marv, attempts to do so, but finds


himself face to face with a number of


challenges. He squares off against


Zanzibar loyalists, Running Man, Four


Horsemen, Jungle Evil, Night Fright, and


Red Blaster. Red Blaster, an elite


assassin with a pinchant for explosives,


is known for trapping his targets in


tight kill zones before finishing them


off with his ever ready grenades. The


four horsemen, a deadly assassination


unit comprised of former SAS operatives,


specialize in close quarters combat and


are feared for their lethal efficiency

a master of jungle warfare. Nightfright,


the last surviving member of the


legendary whisper unit, uses advanced

from the shadows with unmatched


precision. Running man, a disgraced


Olympic sprinter, turned his


record-breaking speed into a weapon,


joining a European group and becoming


nearly impossible to catch. Snake takes


them all down and in a feat that defies


the odds, brings down a hind gunship.


With the help of Holly White and Master


Miller, who's in contact with him over


the radio, Snake manages to find the

English. As such, Snake is faced with

meet Gustava, and along the way, the

Madgar, and Gustava make their way to

Desperate to conclude the mission and to

fights through the facility to make it

makes it to the location where Dr. Marv


is supposedly being held captive. He


realizes that he's just too late. Dr.


Marv, already weakened by heart disease,

to work to retrieve the formula of

A repentant Madnar tells him of Metal


Gear D's weakness. Right before Snake


finds himself engaged in another battle


with the bipeedal tank, piloted once


again by Gray Fox. Snake manages to use


his newfound knowledge to take the metal


gear down. But while he is distracted,


Grey Fox extracts the Olex formula from

confronts Big Boss, Madnar seizes the


moment to slip away from the fortress.


Snake follows in pursuit, traversing a


deadly minefield. Snake also learns that


he was once engaged to Gustava. Gray Fox


and Snake engage in an intense,


thrilling battle. This is one of the


most epic scenes in the entire Metal


Gear history where two best friends were


forced to fight off against each other


due to a changing times and situations.


Eventually, Snake is successful in


defeating Fox and retrieving the Olex


formula. Grey Fox seemingly dies and as


he does, Snake comforts him in his final


moments, telling him that Gustava is


waiting for him on the other side. By


now, you probably know better than to


expect a clean ending. This is Metal


Gear after all. Just when Snake thinks


that the mission is finally over, a


chillingly familiar voice cuts through

the tension rises, Miller calls in over

is a monster. Hardly a revelation given


Cass's awareness of his history of


betrayal and well, the double dealing.


Big Boss responds with a quiet, almost


reflective tone, telling Snake that such


nightmares never truly fade. Big Boss


tells Snake that soldiers can never


truly find peace or live ordinary lives.


The battlefield is the only place they


truly belong. He knows this better than


anyone, which is why he's devoted


himself entirely to building a perfect


refuge for warriors. Quote, "It doesn't


matter who wins here. Our fight will


continue. The loser will be liberated


from the battlefield and the survivor


will live out the rest of his days as a


soldier. He said in a thrilling


climactic battle, Snake manages to


defeat Big Boss, apparently finally


killing him with a makeshift


flamethrower. Him and Holly White fight


their way through the facility to their


extraction point where they finally


leave Zanzibar Land, leaving behind the

and the deactivation of the Metal Gear G


project. After the mission concludes and


the Olex formula is confirmed to be


authentic, Colonel Campbell offers Snake


to rejoin Foxhound. Snake refuses and


goes to Alaska, not to be heard from for


many years to come. It's worth noting


that sometime after the Zanzibar Land


disturbance, or around the time Snake


confronts Big Boss, it's revealed that


Big Boss is Snake's father. The exact


moment of this revelation is unclear,


but it seemingly plays a pivotal role in


Snake's decision to abandon everything


and retreat into a life of solitude. In


the aftermath, Master Miller relocates


to Alaska while the Patriots secure the


bodies of both Big Boss and Grey Fox


from Zanzibar Land. Behind the scenes,


they begin meticulously recording the


events of Metal Gear and Metal Gear 2


Solid Snake. Information they intend to


use to shape future operations and


counter anything or anyone that might


move against them. So, what was the real


Big Boss's goal behind launching two


uprisings? One near South Africa through


his Phantom in Metal Gear and the other


in Zanzibar Land during Metal Gear 2


Solid Snake. Well, the former acted as a


distraction, but both were rooted in his


war against the patriots. He sought to


free the world from their control. But


his vision was deeply flawed. Rather


than pursuing true peace, Big Boss aimed


to create a system where war would never


end, where constant conflict and the


fires of war would sustain an endless


cycle of violence. In his mind, this


perpetual battlefield would give


soldiers a place to belong. But in


reality, it meant replacing one


oppressive system with another equally


destructive one. As Metal Gear 2: Solid


Snake came out before Cojima began


assigning explicit thematic titles to


his games, we can nonetheless deduce its


central theme as war. The story portrays


how Big Boss's ego-driven battle against


the Patriots and pursuit of absolute


freedom from the system made him a


wararmonger only to be brought down by


his own son. For Solid Snake, the ordeal


was deeply scarring. Confronting and


killing Big Boss left him devastated,


bordering on PTSD. Though he claimed to


have freed himself from his nightmares


by the game's end, the truth was far


harsher. War was not done with him, and


it would soon consume him once more. And


that wraps up chapter 7. In the next


chapter, Solid Snake will face his arch


nemesis, his own brother, Liquid Snake.


Things are about to heat up, so buckle


in.


In chapter 7 of our recap of the Metal


Gear Saga, we looked at Solid Snake's


confrontation with big boss in Metal


Gear 2 Solid Snake and how the events in


that game led him into retirement. In


chapter 8, we will talk about how he's


pulled back into the action once again


and the beginning of the long-running


conflict between him and his brother


Liquid Snake. Before we dive into the


main story, let's look at how Cojima


came to develop Metal Gear Solid. In an


interview with Weekly Famitsu number


403, September 6th, 1996, transcribed by


Tumblr user The Archound, he explained


his reasons for reviving the Metal Gear


series, which had last appeared in 1990


with Metal Gear 2 Solid Snake. Quote,


"The truth is that Metal Gear was


actually the first game that I've made


when I've joined Konami. There's that


emotional attachment as well as a


feeling of tension of being seen or not


by the enemy that was characteristic of


Metal Gear that I wanted to explore


further. For example, let's say your


character hides under a desk. When that


happens, the point of view changes to


under the desk and the nearby soldiers


will walk around making noises or you


hear the footsteps of a soldier, so you


quickly hide in a locker to avoid making


noises. I wanted to express that kind of


tension. I had the same concept with the


original Metal Gear, but I wasn't able


to express it with the hardware


available at the time. However, we


finally have a 32-bit console capable of


using many polygons, so I can finally do


what I wanted to do. Cojima explained in


his interview with Gamers Today, Cojima


also explained that the word solid was


more than just a nod to Snake's code


name or the title of the second MSX2


game. It symbolized the series entering


its third chapter while also marking a


dramatic shift, evolving from the flat


world of 2D into the depth and realism


of 3D graphics. With that vision


established, Cojima set the stage for a


new kind of cinematic stealth adventure,


one that would redefine the series as


Metal Gear Solid and introduce players


to its unforgettable story.


It's 2005,


6 years since the fateful events that


took place in Zanzibar Land, where Solid


Snake faced off against his mentor and


father, Big Boss, and came out


victorious. You could be forgiven for


thinking that with Big Boss out of the


picture, at least for now, things are


only going to get better. That, however,


could not be further from the truth.


Even though Solid Snake fought and won


against the fallen legend, the worst is


still to come and things are definitely


not going to get better. Middle Gear


Solid takes place on an island near


Alaska, one of the United States most


critical sites because it secretly


houses a massive nuclear weapons


development facility. In 2005, word


reached US leadership that the island


had been seized by a group calling


itself the sons of big boss. Led by


Liquid Snake Eli, who after the Phantom


Pain served with the SAS before


disappearing, Foxhound has gone rogue


with the support of Psycho Mantis,


Sniper Wolf, Decoy Octopus, Revolver


Ocelot, Vulcan Raven, and an army of


genome soldiers genetically enhanced


with Big Boss's DNA. Liquid now holds


the island firmly under his control. His


demands are simple and a bit hard to


swallow. The sons of Big Boss inform the


US government that it has 24 hours to


cough up a ransom of $1 billion as well


as the remains of Big Boss himself. If


the demands are not met, they will


launch a nuclear attack. Thanks to the


sensitive nature of the mission, the


fact that genetic experiments on Chino


soldiers were a state secret, and the


fact that the DNA in Big Boss's remains


is extremely valuable, the government


decides that it cannot give into these


demands. What's more, the Start 3


Accords are to be signed by several


nations, including the US, in just a


day, and they cannot risk their


non-compliance with non-prololiferation


becoming public knowledge just before


that happens. And as such, Colonel Roy


Campbell is asked by Jim Houseman, the


United States Secretary of Defense, to


convince the now legendary soldier,


Solid Snake, to come out of retirement


in order to deal with this new threat.


The Colonel is somehow able to convince


Snake, while also telling him that he's


involved in this mission for his own


personal reasons. His niece, rookie


soldier Merryill Silverberg, is also


among the hostages on the island. Former


Foxhound medical chief Naomi Hunter


injects Snake with what are known as


nanom machines to increase his combat


capabilities. And without further ado,


Snake is inserted on site. So what are


nanom machines? Nanomachines exist in


the saga to network the soldier, turning


a person's body into a readable,


regulatable node on a battlefield grid.


They justify the series's diioetic


systems, codec, mission tracking, vital


monitoring, while enabling permissions


and control, ID locked weapons, trigger


locks, behavioral gates, and biological


exploits like Foxy, which we'll talk


about later on. In the future, they will


scale into an infrastructure that lets


organizations meter, monetize, and


micromanage war, collapsing logistics,


communications, and compliance into the


bloodstream. But let's not talk about


that just yet. Before we move ahead,


though, it's critical to explain what


the genome project is. It was


essentially the Patriots attempt to


bottle the essence of Big Boss and


mass-produce it. After Ocelot referenced


the research in Portable Ops, the data


became the foundation for Dr. Clark's


genome soldier program. Using Big Boss's


DNA from his supposed dead body,


scientists isolated more than 60 genetic


traits, ranging from heightened reflexes


and combat awareness to raw tactical


instinct that were believed to make him


the ultimate soldier. These traits were


then grafted onto members of the Next


Generation Special Forces, a unit


originally created to counter threats


involving nuclear, biological, and


chemical weapons. At first, they were a


specialized anti-terrorism team built


out of technical and biochemical


experts. But when they were added, the


mercenaries who once served under Big


Boss and Outer Heaven, the unit changed


entirely. The military had simply bought


out the contracts of his former private


guard and merged them with VR trained


recruits, transforming them into


something more dangerous. What emerged


was a brotherhood of genetically


enhanced soldiers. On the surface, they


looked like disciplined professionals.


Their files showed perfect psychological


evaluations, and they were treated as


model troops, but beneath that was a


shared identity. They were sons of big


boss, bonded by the gene therapy that


made them all more alike than brothers.


The rogue Foxhound unit was no ordinary


terrorist cell. It was a collection of


operatives whose abilities bordered on


the supernatural. Raven was said to be


Athapascin, descended from the same


people as the Apaches and the Navajos of


New Mexico. Beyond lineage, Raven was a

code is a parameter that defines exactly


what that information is. Realizing


this, Ryden understands. By analyzing


the program, they might finally uncover


where the Patriots truly operate. As for


Ryden, he chooses to step away from the


battlefield, reconciling with Rose as


the two resolve to build a real life


together. If it sounds like it's all


over, well, it's not. In a postredit


scene, it's revealed that Snake and


Oticon managed to successfully track


down the identities of the 12 members of


the Wise Men's Committee thanks to the


disc containing the virus, with one of


them being one of the contributors to


philanthropy. As it turns out, all 12


leaders of the Patriots have been dead


for nearly a century, meaning that Snake


has lost the only lead he had in the


investigation on the Patriots. However,


Snake concludes that the data is fake.


And he's right. The so-called Wiseman's


Committee were the original


philosophers, a group that no longer


exists, having long since been replaced


by the Patriots, as we've noted in


previous chapters. As for the biggest


contributor, it's never explicitly


stated, but it's reasonable to assume


that the Patriots were using


philanthropy to further their own goals.


By attributing funds under the name of a


long deadad member of the wise men's


committee, they played a double game,


misleading philanthropy while secretly


advancing their own agenda. Now, there


are still questions that need to be


answered to fully grasp what's


happening. The first, why did Ames die


so suddenly? To understand that, it's


important to remember that Richard Ames


was once Natasha Romanenko's husband.


After MGS1's events, Natasha published a


book exposing the truth behind the


incident and in doing so drew attention


to the existence of the Patriots. As a


Patriots agent, Ames might have been


expected to silence her, but instead he


did the opposite, indirectly protecting


her by providing data on Fox die. In the


end, the Patriots switched off Ames'


pacemaker because he had become a


liability within their own S3 operation.


His death not only tied off a loose end,


but also conveniently served the S3


scenario that they were orchestrating.


With his past connections to Natasha and


the data he leaked, Ames posed too great


of a risk of exposing the big shell


plan. So, killing him was nothing more


than a preemptive damage control. And


why did Ocelot kill President Johnson?


After Johnson revealed the truth about


the Patriots to Ryden and even tried to


push Ryden into killing him to stop a


nuclear launch linked to his own vital


sign ID, Oslot intervened and shot him.


Johnson's death neatly eliminated an


unpredictable insider and ensured the S3


scenario stayed firmly on track. Also,


was Solidus working off of false


information?


Yes, he believed the patriots were a


council of 12 humans, the so-called wise


men's committee, and intended to uncover


their names and kill them. But as Ocelot


later revealed, the virus disc was


designed to erase every trace of data


related to the Patriots. Since the


organization was already fully AIdriven,


the program acted as a failafe against


threats like Solidus, ensuring he could


never reach the truth.


And that's the story of Metal Gear Solid


2. Like every mainline entry, Cojima


gave this game a central theme. Meme.


Ryden's entire journey is shaped by


false identities and repetitive orders


derived from existing data, raising


questions about what's real and what's


manufactured. Solid Snake is framed as a


villain through false information. While


Solidus Snake's every move turns out to


have been orchestrated by the Patriots.


In the end, the game shows that the


greatest battles aren't won by guns or


courage alone. They're fought through


information, manipulation, and the


control of the individual. I also want


to touch on the thematic parallels


between MGS2 and MGS5. In MGS2, Ryden


begins with an imposed name and identity


carrying the weight of being shaped into


another snake. But by the end, he casts


that away, choosing instead to define


himself on his own terms. In MGS5, the


player is led to believe that they are


Snake or Big Boss 2, only to learn in


the end that they've been playing as his


phantom. The twist forces the players to


shed their own identity and in effect


become Big Boss or Snake themselves. So,


where Ryden's journey in MGS2 is about


finally accepting his own self, MGS5


turns the mirror on us, the players,


asking us to step into the legend of Big


Boss or Snake and carry that identity


forward.


And that's it for chapter 9. And what a


ride. In chapter 10, we'll dive into the


Sons of the Patriot system and follow

some of the greatest battles of his


life.

and Snake. Now, we turn to the final

his failing health. MGS4, unlike the


previous titles, carried enormous hype.


It was buil as the final Metal Gear,


something Kojima himself repeated in


interviews, though another game


eventually followed. This time, however,


it truly felt like the end. Snake is old


in MGS4, a reflection of Kojima's own


thoughts on aging. In a 2008 interview


with Kikitoso, he explained the unusual


source of inspiration.


Quote, "Yes, especially for Metal Gear


Solid 4, it was very important. So, I


deliberately kind of matched myself and


Old Snake. This is not just the message


to the users, but also a message to the


internal development staff as well.


We've all been working for quite a long


time and I wanted to show that Hideoko


Kojima at 45 still working in the


spotlight. I wanted to show that to the


staff. Kojima stated, quote, I want


users to play and take back some


feelings from my games. Snake is of


course a hero and it's a very very rare


that a fictional hero gets very old or


ages. Normally in games, the hero


doesn't age so much. However, I wanted


to show that everything in the industry


evolves. The games, the platforms, and


even the users who used to play my games


have all aged, and I wanted to express


that in Old Snake. I wanted the users to


almost overlap their experience to say,


quote, I aged. Snake aged. I wanted to


express this feeling in MGS4, he further


added. With Kojima's perspective on


aging setting the tone for Snake's final


mission, it's important to pause and


address two key clarifications before

So, did you really think we'd finish

Gear Rising Revengeance? Of course not.


In chapter 10, we saw the legendary


Solid Snake finally step away from the


battlefield, choosing a life of peace.


But things aren't nearly as calm for our


Jack the Ripper. In chapter 11, we'll


dive into the events that unfolds after


the ending of Guns of the Patriots. Much


like Portable Ops, the canon status of


Revengeance is often debated thanks to


some confusing statements from Hideok


Khojima himself. In an interview with


Outside Xbox, when asked if the game was


truly canon, Kojima once again gave one


of his trademark ambiguous answers.


Quote, first of all, I just want to say


that Metal Gear Rising is a spin-off


focused on Ryden and his story as well


as a particular type of gameplay unique


to this game. So that said, you know, as


far as the setting is concerned, it


takes place after Metal Gear Solid 4. So


in that sense, it's a continuation of


the saga and a continuation of the story


after Guns of the Patriots, he stated.


But then he explained that Revengeance


was Platinum's interpretation of the


story. If he had developed a follow-up


to MGS4 himself, the narrative would


have been taken a very different


direction. Quote, "This time, we're


working with Platinum Games, and it's


being developed outside of the studio.


So, it's a little bit different from the


story that I had in mind for what would


happen after Guns of the Patriots. It's


kind of Platinum Games' interpretation


of the story and their interpretation of


the Metal Gear world. So, in that sense,


I guess you could say that it's sort of


a parallel story at the same time, as


well as a continuation, but it's


Platinum's take on the Metal Gear


universe," Kojima added. So, yes, pretty


confusing, but there is nothing in


Revengeance that goes against the


series's main lore. So, it's safe to


consider it as a continuation saga,


despite it being a spin-off. But before


Revengeance happened, it wasn't even


called that. It was supposed to be


called Metal Gear Solid Rising, a game


set between the events of MGS2 and MGS4,


something we already briefly spoke about


in chapter 10. That game was eventually


changed due to a wide variety of reasons


and was later reinstated as Metal Gear


Rising Revengeance.


Metal Gear Rising Revengeance may not


have been a Hideo Khjima game, and it


may not be the tactical espionage action


experience that the Metal Gear series


has built its identity around, but


Platinum Games' action title was an


excellent game nonetheless, and one that


fans still look back on fondly. The


game's biggest hook, of course, was its


fast-paced slicing and dicing action,


and for good reason. There's nothing


else quite like a good combat system


made by Platinum. But true to the Metal


Gear series, it also had a really


engaging story. Not as heavily cinematic


maybe, and definitely much sillier in


tone, which is really saying something,


but more than serviceable at what it set


out to do. And here, we're going to take
